<Text>This place has pastries.

Tried both the pumpkin and red bean with mochi pastries. The pumpkin was fresh made, not canned and not like pumpkin pie but like kombucha--a light sweetness.

The red bean with mochi filling was very sweet, in a good way, with a wonderful, glutinous mouthfeel.

Also came for their thick and thin green onion pancakes. Both are good--the thin ones are more about the crispy texture, the thick ones are more about the green onions flavor.

The show stoppers were the pork belly bun and their green leek pastry which was a giant empanada stuffed with green onions, vermicelli, egg, and ground meat. Yum!<//Text>< pics>

<name>David Lin<//name>< Text>
I took the kids for Saturday breakfast.  We used to get soy milk, egg pancake, rice roll in OC from 99 Ranch and this seems to be the only place to get soy milk for breakfast.

We were disappointed in the experience.  The soy milk tasted diluted, both the hot and cold one.  My 5 year old's comment is 'this tastes like water'.

The fried dough inside the rice roll was pretty tough instead of crunchy.  The egg pancake was good, the texture is more doughy than normal.

We came here for dinner awhile back, similar luke warm impression on food.  The restaurant is very cluttered, and as expected of old restaurant, you wondee about cleaniness.

The servers are nice, but when there are more than 3 tables, they seem to get overwhelm and get anxious at each other.<//Text>

< rating>
4</rating>
< text>
The Food
One of the more decent Hong Kong style cafe around south bay area is Venus Cafe. I had a few of their dishes like their Signature Baked Item and Guilin Rice Noodle Soup, as well as Dessert. This time around I got their Seafood Combo Guilin Rice Noodle Soup. I've also had their Beef Brisket Guilin Rice Noodle Soup. Both were very good, and I especially like the noodles. The Seafood Combo comes with fish, squid, and shrimp, with a nice touch of peanut and pickled veggie.

The Miscellaneous
Venus Cafe is within a plaza with a decent sized parking lot. The restaurant itself is average in size, but the seatings are well arranged. The service is normal, and the employees are quite quick and efficient. One thing I like about the restaurant is their menu. They have quite the extensive menu with lots of selections. But the menu itself is also designed well. The price of all their dishes are fairly reasonable. Will return again sometime to eat more of their menu...a good place to visit.<//text>

<review>I missed this place when it was in Cupertino. I drove an hour in traffic to come here.

Milktea - it's the next best thing from having it in HK

Shrimp paste beef fried rice - like every restaurant, they need to put not shrimp paste in it.  It'll make a huge difference.

Black pepper pork chop fried instant noodles in an iron skillet - my son's favorite, I had a bite and it was very good.  Enough black pepper flavor, noodle was dry. It was really good.

My special pork chop baked over rice was good but I didn't like the white sauce, it taste starchy. The red sauce was good.  You can actually request all red sauce.  The difference of this pork chop is that it's deep fried pork cutlet not the regular pork chop.

This is definitely the place to be for reminiscent HK comfort food.</review><Time>1575434790675< /Time></record>

<time>1571118727143< /time>< review>
Awesome experience to try Hong Kong cuisine that blends both Eastern and Western elements. For those not from Hong Kong, I got spaghetti, pork chop, a chicken wing and an egg. Each item sounds like American food yet it still had an Asian flavor somehow.

The other dish is more of a hybrid. American Macaroni and ham (or is this British) in ramen broth.

The $25 limit to use a credit card seemed a bit high if you have a party of two or fewer ("fewer" of course being just me wandering in by myself). I was expecting a $20 limit. Either way, I'm looking forward to going back to try more dishes.</review>

< review>
This would be my go-to HK cafe in San Jose! It's kind of far but I try to go whenever I'm close. It's located in the plaza with 99 Ranch and Gen, and most of the time it's really hard to find parking.

There are not that many good HK cafes in SJ so I really recommend trying Venus! I usually get either their pork chop with spaghetti & bolognaise sauce OR their seafood stir-fried udon (my favorite!!) it's always so good everytime I come. I also love, love, love HK desserts!! I would always get their sago desserts, with their different kinds of fruits. The fruits are always fresh, the dessert isn't too sweet, definitely satisfies my meal there.</review>

<Text>I have been here many times. They have been around for a number of years. They specialized in Hong Kong fast food. And I think they have done a decent job at it. For those who aren't familiar with HK fast food, it's usually a lot of carbs, fast to make or already made, and is heavily influenced by the West while maintaining the Chinese characteristics. The combination of cooking style provides a very unique experience. But don't expect it to be healthy. If you grew up with it, it's comfort food. If you are new to it, it will be an acquired taste.

Pros:
1. Open very late. Great place to get food after 10 PM.
2. A lot of variety.
3. Decent Asian dessert selection.
4. A Chinese place that has cheese dishes, and I don't mean grilled cheese.
4. Very reasonable price.
5. There is a decent size parking lot in front of it.
6. In the same strip mall as Ranch 99, you can do your grocery shopping before or after your dining experience.

Cons:
1. Mostly carb based plates.
2. A lot of greasy plates as well.
3. Parking lot is always full, hard to get parking.

If you are new to this style of places, it will give you a very unique experience. If you miss your HK fast food/street food experience, this is a good place to satisfy your craving.

The missing star is the service. The overall service is decent. But when you asked if they have any other vegetables, the usually reply is "we got everything except veggie x." Their menu only have 1 dish with green leaf veggie in it and it's the bak choy. So getting that kind of reply doesn't really help much as I was checking to see if there are different green leaf veggie dishes. It would be much helpful if they can at least provide some green leaf dish's names. Or recommend something.</Text><pics>None</pics><Resp>None<//Resp>< gmapID>
0x808fcc17216805ab:0x7274b1678106cb65< /gmapID>

< Text>
If you don't have a Cost Co card, your wasting money. Gasoline is going up but CostCo offers some of the best savings. These savings off set the membership fee and you come out a winner. So you get the savings and money back, win win.< /Text>
